**Human:**

Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, and the hungarian-vat skill (SKILL.md + 
references/architecture.md) before writing anything. This session is Phase 3, 
step 1: scaffold the entire solution as a walking skeleton. Structure only — 
no VAT business logic yet (no parsers, no validation rules, no strategy math). 
That comes in the next session.

DELIVERABLES OF THIS SESSION

1. Repository layout exactly as defined in references/architecture.md:
   - VatDesk.sln with src/VatDesk.Core, src/VatDesk.Infrastructure, 
     src/VatDesk.Api (.NET 8), tests/VatDesk.Tests (xUnit)
   - frontend/ — React 18 + TypeScript via Vite, with the folder conventions 
     from the skill (src/api/types.ts placeholder included)
   - Enforce the dependency direction in the .csproj references: 
     Api → Infrastructure → Core; Core references nothing external.

2. Walking skeleton that proves every seam works end to end:
   - EF Core + Npgsql wired, DbContext with the four tables from the skill's 
     persistence schema (entities + initial migration; migrations auto-apply 
     on startup)
   - GET /api/health returning app version + DB connectivity status
   - One placeholder Core abstraction file per interface named in the skill 
     (IInvoiceParser, IVatCategoryRegistry, IVatDeclarationStrategy, 
     IReportRenderer) — signatures only, no implementations
   - DI registration pattern for country strategies stubbed 
     (AddCountry<TRegistry,TStrategy>("HU") compiles, registers nothing real yet)
   - Frontend: minimal App shell that calls /api/health and renders the result; 
     Vite dev proxy configured to the API
   - One xUnit test that reads .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/sample-clean.csv 
     from disk and asserts it has 10 data rows — this only proves test 
     infrastructure + fixture path resolution work; no parsing logic.

3. Tooling and hygiene:
   - .gitignore covering .NET, node, Vite, IDE files, .env; verify no bin/obj/ 
     node_modules get staged
   - .editorconfig with sensible C#/TS defaults
   - Dockerfile (multi-stage: node build → dotnet publish → runtime, API serving 
     the built frontend) and docker-compose.yml with the app + postgres:16, 
     healthcheck on postgres, env-var-based connection string, no secrets 
     committed
   - README.md skeleton with sections (leave TODO markers where content comes 
     later): Overview, Quick start (docker compose up), Demo credentials, 
     Architecture, Security, Extending to a new country, AI-assisted workflow

ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA — verify each yourself before finishing:
- dotnet build succeeds with zero warnings-as-errors issues
- dotnet test passes
- docker compose up brings up postgres + app; /api/health reports DB connected
- npm run dev in frontend/ shows the health status from the API
- git status is clean of ignored artifacts

CONSTRAINTS
- Follow every naming and layering rule in the skill exactly; if anything in the 
  skill and this prompt conflict, the skill wins — tell me about the conflict 
  instead of silently choosing.
- If a decision isn't covered by the skill or PLAN.md, make the boring, 
  conventional choice and note it in a "Decisions made" list at the end.
- Conventional commits. Commit in logical units as you go (structure, backend 
  skeleton, frontend skeleton, docker, docs) — not one giant commit.
- When done: update the Phase 3 line in docs/PLAN.md to "in progress — skeleton 
  complete" in the final commit, and give me a summary of what exists, what's 
  stubbed, and what the next session should tackle.

**Human:**

[Result: 1	# VATDesk Architecture & Conventions
2	
3	## Stack
4	
5	- Backend: ASP.NET Core 8 (LTS) Web API, EF Core + Npgsql, QuestPDF (Community license).
6	- Frontend: React 18 + TypeScript + Vite, served as static files by the API in
7	  production (single deployable unit).
8	- DB: PostgreSQL. Migrations applied automatically on startup.
9	- Packaging: multi-stage Dockerfile (node build → dotnet build → runtime image);
10	  docker-compose adds Postgres. Deployment target: Azure (Web App for Containers...]

**Human:**

[Result: 1	# VATDesk Input Data Contract
2	
3	Two input formats are supported. Format is decided by content sniffing: a file whose
4	first non-whitespace character is `<` is treated as XML; otherwise CSV is attempted.
5	Extension is a hint, never the decider.
6	
7	## 1. CSV contract
8	
9	- Encoding: UTF-8 (accept BOM). Delimiter: comma. Header row **required**.
10	- Decimal separator: `.` — parse with invariant culture. Reject `,` decimals as a
11	  row error with a helpful message ("use 27000.50, not 27...]

**Claude:**

## Summary

Phase 3 walking skeleton is complete and verified — all acceptance criteria pass: `dotnet build` (0 warnings/errors), `dotnet test` (1/1 passing), `docker compose up` (postgres healthy, migrations auto-apply, `/api/health` reports DB connected, frontend served at root), `npm run dev` (Vite proxy → API → DB round-trips), and `git status` is clean with no build artifacts staged. 5 commits, in logical units.

**What exists:**
- `VatDesk.sln` with `src/VatDesk.Core` → `VatDesk.Infrastructure` → `VatDesk.Api` (.NET 8), `tests/VatDesk.Tests` (xUnit), `frontend/` (React 18 + TS + Vite) — layering enforced by project references, Core has zero external deps.
- Core: `TransactionLine`, `VatCategory`, `DeclarationSummary` models; `Direction`/`VatKind`/`UserRole`/`SourceFormat`/`DeclarationStatus` enums; `ValidationIssue` + `Severity` + rule-id constants (V1–V8); the four abstraction interfaces (`IInvoiceParser`, `IVatCategoryRegistry`, `IVatDeclarationStrategy`, `IReportRenderer`) as signatures only.
- Infrastructure: `VatDeskDbContext` with the four persistence tables (snake_case columns, enum-to-string conversions, FKs/indexes matching the skill's schema exactly), initial EF migration, and a generic `AddCountry<TRegistry,TStrategy>("HU")` DI stub (not yet called — no real HU implementation exists).
- Api: `GET /api/health` (version + DB connectivity via `CanConnectAsync`), migrations auto-apply on startup, serves the built frontend as static files (single deployable unit).
- Frontend: minimal App shell with loading/error/success states calling `/api/health`, `src/api/types.ts` mirroring the DTO, Vite dev proxy to the API.
- Docker: multi-stage Dockerfile (node build → dotnet publish → aspnet runtime), `docker-compose.yml` (app + postgres:16 with healthcheck, env-var connection string, `.env.example` for local overrides).
- `.gitignore`, `.editorconfig`, README skeleton with TODO markers, `docs/PLAN.md` Phase 3 line updated to "in progress — skeleton complete."

**What's stubbed / intentionally missing (next session):**
- No CSV/XML parsers, no HU category registry or declaration strategy, no PDF renderer, no validation rule implementations — `AddCountry<...>("HU")` is never invoked because there's nothing real to register yet.
- No auth (JWT/roles) — connection string env var is wired but no `Jwt__Key` yet since there's no auth code.
- Declarations/countries controllers don't exist yet — only `HealthController`.

**Decisions made (not specified in skill/plan, boring defaults chosen):**
- EF Core/Npgsql pinned to `8.0.11` (matches Npgsql's own dependency graph, avoids an MSB3277 version-conflict warning).
- Migrations tooling: `Microsoft.EntityFrameworkCore.Design` referenced by both Infrastructure and Api (standard `dotnet ef` pattern with `--startup-project`).
- Added `public partial class Program;` to `Program.cs` — standard boilerplate enabling `WebApplicationFactory<Program>` for integration tests in a later session.
- Dev-only default Postgres connection string in `appsettings.json` (`vatdesk`/`vatdesk` on localhost) — not a real secret, overridden by env var in Docker/Azure, consistent with the "no secrets committed" rule.

**No conflicts found** between the skill, `docs/PLAN.md`, and this prompt — architecture.md's file layout, persistence schema, and interface list were followed exactly.

**Next session should tackle:** CSV parser (`CsvInvoiceParser`) + NAV XML parser (with the mandated XXE hardening) against the skill's sample fixtures, `HungarianVatCategoryRegistry` + `HungarianVatDeclarationStrategy` with the V1–V8 validation rules, wiring `AddCountry<...>("HU")` for real, and the `POST /api/declarations` upload endpoint — using the golden values in `data-contract.md` as the test oracle.

**Human:**

Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, and the full hungarian-vat skill — SKILL.md plus 
ALL THREE reference files (data-contract.md, vat-categories.md, architecture.md) — 
before writing code. This session completes Phase 3: the entire backend domain, 
from file bytes to PDF, on top of the existing skeleton. Do not touch frontend/ 
beyond regenerating API types if you maintain them there.

Work in four stages, in order. Each stage ends with: tests green, one conventional 
commit, brief progress note. Do not start a stage before the previous one is green.

STAGE A — Category registry + canonical model + validation engine
- Implement VatCategory, VatKind, and HungarianVatCategoryRegistry exactly per 
  references/vat-categories.md (codes, kinds, rates, HU/EN display names, sort order).
- Implement TransactionLine and ValidationIssue per data-contract.md.
- Implement the validation engine: rules V1–V8 with the exact severities and the 
  ±1 HUF tolerance from the skill. Rules must be individually testable units, 
  ordered execution, each issue carrying row number, rule id, severity, and a 
  message with expected vs actual values.
- Tests: one test class per rule with passing and failing cases. Registry test: 
  exactly 8 codes, kinds and rates correct.

STAGE B — Parsers
- CsvInvoiceParser and NavXmlInvoiceParser per data-contract.md: header matching 
  rules, invariant culture, ISO dates, direction defaulting, XML element mapping, 
  vatPercentage→code mapping, vatExemption handling, inherited invoice header 
  fields, SourceRowNumber tracking.
- ParserFactory with content sniffing (first non-whitespace '<' ⇒ XML), extension 
  is only a hint.
- XML hardening is non-negotiable: DtdProcessing.Prohibit, XmlResolver = null, 
  character cap. Add a test that feeds an XML with a DOCTYPE/external entity and 
  asserts it is rejected.
- Tests parse the canonical fixtures from .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/: 
  sample-clean.csv ⇒ 10 valid rows, zero issues; sample-invalid.csv ⇒ assert the 
  specific rule id triggered per row (each dirty row targets exactly one rule); 
  sample-nav.xml ⇒ 3 lines with correct codes including the TAM exemption line.

STAGE C — Declaration strategy + persistence
- HungarianVatDeclarationStrategy: aggregate error-free rows into 
  DeclarationSummary per data-contract.md section 5 (per-category × direction 
  totals, totalOutputVat, totalDeductibleInputVat, netVatPayable; warning rows 
  included in totals, error rows excluded; declared amounts used, never computed).
- Golden-value test: processing sample-clean.csv yields EXACTLY the table in 
  data-contract.md section 6 — outputVat 94300, inputVat 50600, netVatPayable 
  43700, and every per-category cell. If your numbers differ, your code is wrong, 
  not the skill.
- Persist Declaration + category totals + validation issues via the existing 
  schema; raw rows are NOT stored. Status: Completed / CompletedWithWarnings / 
  Failed per whether warnings/errors occurred.

STAGE D — PDF + API endpoints
- QuestPdfReportRenderer per the PDF section in architecture.md: A4, header, 
  summary cards, category table OUT-block then IN-block, validation summary, 
  disclaimer footer, page numbers. Community license configuration.
- Endpoints per architecture.md: POST /api/declarations (multipart, 5MB cap, 
  processes, persists, returns summary DTO), GET /api/declarations, 
  GET /api/declarations/{id}, GET /api/declarations/{id}/pdf (stream, correct 
  content type), GET /api/countries/{cc}/vat-categories.
- No auth in this session — leave endpoints anonymous with a TODO(Phase5) marker; 
  auth is the next phase and I don't want it half-done here.
- Controllers stay thin: validate → delegate → map. Any business rule found in a 
  controller is a defect.
- ProblemDetails for all error paths; unparseable file ⇒ 400 with a clear message, 
  not a 500.
- Integration-style test (WebApplicationFactory): upload sample-clean.csv, assert 
  200 with the golden totals; download PDF, assert non-empty application/pdf.

ACCEPTANCE — run all of it yourself before finishing:
- dotnet build + dotnet test fully green
- docker compose up, then via curl: upload sample-clean.csv ⇒ golden totals in the 
  JSON; upload sample-invalid.csv ⇒ CompletedWithWarnings/errors surfaced with rule 
  ids; upload the XXE test file ⇒ rejected; fetch the PDF ⇒ valid file
- No decimal→double anywhere (grep for 'double' in amount paths)

CONSTRAINTS
- Skill wins over this prompt on any conflict — surface the conflict, don't 
  reconcile silently.
- Uncovered decisions: boring conventional choice + "Decisions made" list at end.
- Finish by updating docs/PLAN.md Phase 3 to complete (checkbox) in the final 
  commit, and give me: what was built, test count, any deviations, and what 
  Phase 4 needs from the API contract (paste the final DTO shapes).

**Human:**

[Result: 1	# VATDesk Input Data Contract
2	
3	Two input formats are supported. Format is decided by content sniffing: a file whose
4	first non-whitespace character is `<` is treated as XML; otherwise CSV is attempted.
5	Extension is a hint, never the decider.
6	
7	## 1. CSV contract
8	
9	- Encoding: UTF-8 (accept BOM). Delimiter: comma. Header row **required**.
10	- Decimal separator: `.` — parse with invariant culture. Reject `,` decimals as a
11	  row error with a helpful message ("use 27000.50, not 27...]

[Result: 1	# VAT Category Registry
2	
3	## Model
4	
5	```csharp
6	enum VatKind { Percentage, ZeroRated, Exempt, ReverseCharge }
7	
8	record VatCategory(
9	    string Code,            // stable identifier used in files, DB, API, UI
10	    VatKind Kind,
11	    decimal? Rate,          // only for Percentage/ZeroRated (0m for ZeroRated)
12	    string DisplayNameHu,
13	    string DisplayNameEn,
14	    int SortOrder);
15	
16	interface IVatCategoryRegistry
17	{
18	    string CountryCode { get; }          // "HU...]

[Result: 1	# VATDesk Architecture & Conventions
2	
3	## Stack
4	
5	- Backend: ASP.NET Core 8 (LTS) Web API, EF Core + Npgsql, QuestPDF (Community license).
6	- Frontend: React 18 + TypeScript + Vite, served as static files by the API in
7	  production (single deployable unit).
8	- DB: PostgreSQL. Migrations applied automatically on startup.
9	- Packaging: multi-stage Dockerfile (node build → dotnet build → runtime image);
10	  docker-compose adds Postgres. Deployment target: Azure (Web App for Containers...]

**Claude:**

Live testing surfaced a real correctness issue: NAV XML invoices with multiple lines share one `InvoiceNumber` by design (inherited from the header), but my V8 duplicate-detection treats every line after the first as a "duplicate" — which is a false positive for legitimate multi-line invoices. Let me fix this properly.

**Claude:**

## Summary

Phase 3 backend is complete, all four stages green, verified live against `docker compose up` + curl. 6 commits, in stage order.

**What was built** (69 tests, 0 warnings):
- **Stage A**: `HungarianVatCategoryRegistry` (exact 8 codes/kinds/rates/names/order) + `TransactionLineValidator` running V2–V8 as independently testable static checks.
- **Stage B**: `CsvInvoiceParser` (CsvHelper-backed) and `NavXmlInvoiceParser` (hardened: `DtdProcessing.Prohibit`, `XmlResolver = null`, char cap) + `ParserFactory` with content sniffing. Both own V1 (malformed rows are format-specific, can't become a typed `TransactionLine`).
- **Stage C**: `HungarianVatDeclarationStrategy` — golden values match exactly (94,300 / 50,600 / 43,700). `DeclarationRepository` persists aggregates + issues only, no raw rows.
- **Stage D**: `QuestPdfReportRenderer`, `DeclarationsController`, `CountriesController`, global `ProblemDetails` error handling. No auth — anonymous with `TODO(Phase5)` markers.

**Deviations / conflicts surfaced** (per your "skill wins, don't reconcile silently" instruction):
1. `Declaration.UserId` is now nullable — no auth exists this session, so uploads are anonymous. Becomes required in Phase 5.
2. V7 (partner tax number format) is hardcoded HU/EU regex inside the shared validator — `vat-categories.md`'s registry model has no seam for country-specific validation beyond VAT codes. Extending to RO will need this pulled out.
3. Used ASP.NET Core's built-in keyed DI (`[FromKeyedServices("HU")]`) instead of building a dedicated `ICountryResolver` (architecture.md mentions one) — keyed DI already satisfies both the hard-default and the `{cc}`-route-param cases without an extra abstraction.
4. **Real bug caught by live testing, not by unit tests**: NAV XML invoices share one `InvoiceNumber` across all their lines by design, which made V8 (duplicate detection) false-positive on every multi-line XML invoice. Fixed by threading `SourceFormat` into `BuildDeclaration` and skipping V8 for XML sources — documented with a regression test and a code comment explaining why.

**What Phase 4 needs** — final DTO shapes (`frontend/src/api/types.ts` already mirrors these):
```ts
DeclarationDto: { id, sourceFilename, sourceFormat, countryCode, status, createdAt,
  perCategory: CategoryTotalDto[], totalOutputVat, totalDeductibleInputVat, netVatPayable,
  validation: ValidationSummaryDto }
DeclarationListItemDto: { id, sourceFilename, sourceFormat, countryCode, status,
  totalOutputVat, totalDeductibleInputVat, netVatPayable, validRows, warningRows, errorRows, createdAt }
VatCategoryDto: { code, kind, rate, displayNameHu, displayNameEn, sortOrder }
```
Endpoints: `POST /api/declarations` (multipart, field name `file`) → 200 `DeclarationDto`; `GET /api/declarations` → `DeclarationListItemDto[]`; `GET /api/declarations/{id}` → `DeclarationDto`; `GET /api/declarations/{id}/pdf` → `application/pdf`; `GET /api/countries/{cc}/vat-categories` → `VatCategoryDto[]`. All errors are RFC7807 `application/problem+json`.

**Human:**

Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, the hungarian-vat skill (SKILL.md + 
references/architecture.md, especially the security checklist and API surface), 
and study docs/design/ thoroughly — open the exported design for the Login screen 
and the app shell/dashboard before writing any frontend code. This session is the 
first vertical slice of Phase 4: authentication + authorization end-to-end, the 
Login page, and a placeholder Home/Dashboard behind it.

DESIGN FIDELITY COMMITMENT (applies to this and all future frontend sessions)
docs/design/ is the single source of truth for visual output. Concretely:
- Extract the design tokens (colors, typography, spacing, radii, shadows) from 
  the design export into a central theme file (CSS variables or theme object) in 
  this session — every component consumes tokens, never hard-coded values. All 
  future pages will reuse this file, so name and organize it accordingly. Consider using chadcn for this step. Also implement theme light/dark selection with button to change.
- Match the Login screen from the design pixel-conscientiously: layout, hierarchy, 
  the demo-credentials hint box, the secondary "Continue with Microsoft/Google" 
  buttons not needed for now, simply ignore them.
- Implement every state the design defines for login: default, loading (submit 
  pending), invalid credentials error, and validation of empty fields.
- Where the design export includes reusable components (buttons, inputs, cards), 
  build them as shared components in frontend/src/components/ui/ now — the rest 
  of Phase 4 will consume them.
- If something is ambiguous or missing in the design, choose the minimal 
  interpretation consistent with the design's visual language and list it under 
  "Design gaps" at the end — do not invent new visual styles.

STAGE A — Backend auth (replaces the TODO(Phase5) markers)
- Seeded users per the skill: admin@demo.hu / Admin123! (Admin), 
  viewer@demo.hu / Viewer123! (Viewer). Passwords hashed (ASP.NET Identity 
  PasswordHasher or BCrypt) in the seed migration — no plaintext at rest.
- POST /api/auth/login: validates credentials, returns short-lived JWT (HS256, 
  signing key from env var / user-secrets, never committed; fail fast at startup 
  if the key is missing or shorter than 32 bytes) with role claim + display name. 
  Add GET /api/auth/me returning the current principal for session restore.
- Wire authentication + authorization middleware. Role policies per the skill's 
  API table: POST /api/declarations ⇒ Admin only; declaration reads + PDF + 
  vat-categories ⇒ any authenticated user; health stays anonymous.
- Rate limiting on /api/auth/login (tight window) per security checklist item 6.
- 401 vs 403 must be correct and return ProblemDetails.
- Tests: login success (token contains role claim), login failure (401, generic 
  message — never "user not found" vs "wrong password"), Viewer calling POST 
  /api/declarations ⇒ 403, anonymous calling GET /api/declarations ⇒ 401, 
  rate limiter triggers after N rapid attempts.

STAGE B — Frontend auth infrastructure
- Auth context/store: holds token + user (name, role); token kept in memory with 
  sessionStorage persistence for refresh survival — document this tradeoff in a 
  code comment (XSS surface vs UX; acceptable for demo scope).
- API client wrapper: attaches Authorization header, on 401 clears session and 
  redirects to /login preserving the intended destination.
- Route guards: unauthenticated ⇒ /login; role-aware guard component 
  (RequireRole) ready for later pages even though only Admin/any-auth exist now.
- Mirror DTO types from the Phase 3 summary into frontend/src/api/types.ts 
  (auth DTOs added).

STAGE C — Pages
- /login: per the design, per the fidelity commitment above. On success route to 
  intended destination or /.
- / (Home/Dashboard placeholder): app shell from the design — header with app 
  name, user's display name, role badge, logout — and an empty-state content area 
  matching the design's dashboard empty state ("no declarations yet" + a 
  "New declaration" primary button visible ONLY for Admin role, non-functional 
  with "Coming soon" tooltip). This shell (layout, nav, header) must be the 
  reusable frame every subsequent page mounts into.
- Logout: clears session, returns to /login.

ACCEPTANCE — verify yourself:
- dotnet test green including new auth tests; frontend builds with zero TS errors
- docker compose up ⇒ full flow in browser: /login renders per design, wrong 
  password shows error state, admin login lands on dashboard with "New 
  declaration" visible, viewer login hides it, refresh keeps you logged in, 
  logout works, deep link to / while logged out bounces to /login and back after 
  login
- curl: Viewer token POSTing /api/declarations gets 403; no token gets 401

CONSTRAINTS
- Skill wins on conflict; surface conflicts. Boring choices + "Decisions made" 
  list for anything uncovered.
- UI role-gating is cosmetic; server-side policies are the enforcement (skill 
  hard rule). Never skip the server check because the UI hides a button.
- Conventional commits per stage. Final commit: restructure docs/PLAN.md — mark 
  Phase 5 baseline (JWT + roles) as done and folded into this slice, keep 
  "Entra ID (stretch)" as its own unchecked line, and add Phase 4 sub-checkboxes: 
  [x] 4.1 auth+login+shell, [ ] 4.2 upload, [ ] 4.3 report view, [ ] 4.4 
  dashboard/history. End with: what exists, design gaps found, and what 4.2 
  needs.

5

[Result: 1	# Example: Browser-driven web app
2	
3	You have a dev server that serves HTML to a browser. An agent in a
4	headless container can't open a browser window — so "run the app" means
5	launching the dev server, driving a headless Chromium against it, and
6	producing a screenshot that proves the page rendered.
7	
8	Don't write a browser driver. Use `chromium-cli`.
9	
10	## Dev server
11	
12	Find the dev command (`package.json` `scripts.dev`, `Makefile`,
13	README), start it in the background, and ...]

**Claude:**

## Summary

**All acceptance criteria met**: `dotnet test` green (79/79, including new auth tests), frontend builds with zero TS errors, and I verified the full browser flow with Playwright against the actual `docker compose` build (no browser tool was available by default, so I installed one into the scratchpad) — login default/error/validation states, admin vs. viewer dashboards, dark mode, session-refresh persistence, logout, and the deep-link-while-logged-out bounce all work correctly. `curl` confirms Viewer→403 and anonymous→401 on `POST /api/declarations`.

**What exists now:**
- **Backend**: seeded users (hashed passwords, migration-time), `POST /api/auth/login` (JWT, role + display-name claims, generic error message), `GET /api/auth/me`, role policies matching the skill's API table, login rate-limited (8/min/IP), 401/403 as ProblemDetails, fail-fast JWT key validation.
- **Frontend**: Tailwind v4 + design tokens (light matches the export, dark is this session's derivation) with a persisted toggle; shadcn-style primitives in `components/ui/`; `AuthContext` + route guards; `/login` and the app shell + dashboard empty state, both design-matched.

**Real bugs caught by actually running it, not just building it:**
1. `AddCountry`'s keyed-service wiring didn't resolve — .NET DI doesn't thread keyed dependencies through implicit constructor injection.
2. NAV XML's V8 duplicate-detection false-flagged every multi-line invoice (all lines legitimately share one `InvoiceNumber`).
3. Native `disabled` on the "Coming soon" buttons set `pointer-events: none`, silently killing the tooltip for real mouse users, not just Playwright — fixed with `aria-disabled`.

**Design gaps** (my own calls, since the export didn't cover them):
- **Dark mode**: not in the design at all; derived by inverting neutrals, brightening the teal accent for contrast, and lightening status colors.
- **Demo credentials copy**: the mockup was a client-only fake login ("any password works"); ours checks a real password, so the buttons autofill the real demo password and the hint text was adjusted accordingly.
- **`UserEntity.DisplayName`**: not in architecture.md's original `users` schema; added (additive) for the JWT display-name claim and the header/account-menu UI.
- Header's "New declaration" nav item and the dashboard's disabled CTAs use a dimmed/`aria-disabled` treatment not present in the design (there they're fully active) — appropriate since ours are genuinely non-functional this session.

**What 4.2 (upload) needs:** the `POST /api/declarations` contract is already built and tested (multipart, 5 MB cap, `DeclarationDto` response) — the header's "New declaration" and the dashboard's "Create your first declaration" buttons are wired with `RequireRole`/tooltip scaffolding ready to swap from disabled to a real `/upload` route.

---

**Human:**

Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, the hungarian-vat skill (SKILL.md + 
references/data-contract.md for the file rules), and study the Upload screen in 
docs/design/ — including the format hint tabs, sample download links, file card, 
inline error states, and the processing steps (Parsing → Validating → 
Calculating). This session is Phase 4.2: the complete upload flow, wired to the 
existing POST /api/declarations. The design fidelity commitment from 4.1 applies: 
consume the shared theme tokens and ui/ components; extend them if the design 
requires new ones — never fork styles locally.

SCOPE BOUNDARY
The full report view is 4.3. This session ends at a stub: route 
/declarations/:id renders inside the app shell showing declaration id, status 
chip (per design status colors), and a "Full report view coming soon" note. 
Success navigation targets this stub. Do not build summary cards, category 
tables, or the validation panel yet.

STAGE A — Backend: serve the canonical sample files
- Expose GET /api/samples/clean.csv, /api/samples/invalid.csv, 
  /api/samples/nav.xml (any authenticated user), correct Content-Type and 
  Content-Disposition for download.
- Source of truth stays .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/ — do NOT duplicate 
  the files in git. Copy them into the API output (wwwroot/samples or embedded 
  resources) via an MSBuild copy step, and ensure the Dockerfile picks them up. 
  Add a test asserting the served clean.csv is byte-identical to the skill asset.
- Verify POST /api/declarations returns proper ProblemDetails for: oversized 
  file (413 or 400 per existing implementation — keep consistent), unsupported 
  content, empty file. If any of these currently produce a 500, fix the backend 
  and add the missing test — note it under "Decisions made".

STAGE B — Upload page (/declarations/new, Admin-only via RequireRole)
Per the design:
- Drag & drop zone + click-to-browse fallback; accepts .csv/.xml.
- Client-side pre-validation BEFORE upload: >5 MB, empty file, wrong 
  extension/type ⇒ inline error states exactly as designed. Client checks are 
  UX only — the server remains the enforcement (skill hard rule); never assume 
  client validation means the server call can't fail.
- Format hint tabs "CSV" / "NAV 3.0 XML" showing the expected structure per the 
  design (content can be sourced from data-contract.md, abbreviated to what the 
  design shows).
- "Download sample file" links for both formats hitting the Stage A endpoints.
- After file selection: file card (name, size, remove) + "Process" primary 
  button, per design.

STAGE C — Processing + outcomes
- On Process: upload with the API client (auth header from 4.1), show the 
  design's stepped progress state (Parsing → Validating → Calculating). The API 
  is a single call — drive the steps as an indeterminate visual sequence, and be 
  honest in code comments that steps are presentational, not server events.
- Success ⇒ navigate to /declarations/:id stub. Show a success toast with the 
  status (Completed / CompletedWithWarnings) using the design's toast component.
- Failure paths, each with its designed state: 400 unparseable ⇒ the full-failure 
  error screen from the design (message, what to check, links to sample files, 
  "Try again"); 401 ⇒ existing session-expiry redirect; 403 ⇒ "Admins only" 
  notice; network failure ⇒ retryable error toast.
- Wire the dashboard's "New declaration" button (currently "Coming soon") to 
  /declarations/new; keep it Admin-only.

ACCEPTANCE — verify yourself:
- Frontend builds zero TS errors; dotnet test green including the sample-serving 
  and error-shape tests.
- docker compose up, in browser as admin: download both samples from the upload 
  page; upload sample-clean.csv ⇒ progress states ⇒ stub page shows Completed; 
  upload sample-invalid.csv ⇒ stub shows CompletedWithWarnings; drop a 6 MB file 
  ⇒ inline rejection without a network call; rename a .png to .csv and upload ⇒ 
  server-side rejection surfaces the designed error screen.
- As viewer: /declarations/new bounces (route guard) and the dashboard button 
  is absent.

CONSTRAINTS
- Skill wins on conflict; surface conflicts. Boring choices + "Decisions made".
- Conventional commits per stage. Final commit: check off 4.2 in docs/PLAN.md, 
  add any new "Design gaps" found, and end with: what exists, DTO/route additions 
  4.3 will consume, and open questions for the report view.

**Claude:**

## Summary

Phase 4.2 is complete — full upload flow wired end to end, verified with `dotnet test` (87/87 green), a zero-TS-error frontend build, and a Playwright pass against the actual `docker compose` build (screenshots confirmed pixel-level fidelity to the design across every state: dropzone, oversized-file rejection, file card, processing steps, success toast + stub page for both `Completed` and `CompletedWithWarnings`, the full-page error screen, and the viewer route-guard bounce).

**What exists now:**
- **Backend**: `SamplesController` serves the 3 canonical skill assets (byte-identical, tested) via an MSBuild `Content`-copy step — never duplicated in git. All upload error paths (oversized, binary-content-with-.csv-extension, empty, wrong-extension) were empirically verified against real Kestrel to already return clean 400 ProblemDetails — no backend fix was needed.
- **Frontend**: `/declarations/new` (Admin-only) with dropzone, file card, format-hint tabs, presentational processing steps, and full outcome handling (success → stub navigation + toast, 400 → error screen, 403 → notice, network failure → retryable toast); `/declarations/:id` stub; new `ui/` primitives (`Tabs`, `Toast`).

**Decisions made:**
- Oversized/binary/empty/wrong-extension uploads already returned proper 400s — verified via tests, no fix needed (documented in the Stage A commit).
- Sample-serving route reads from `AppContext.BaseDirectory` — confirmed empirically that this resolves correctly under both `WebApplicationFactory` and the real published app.

**Surfaced conflict**: the design's format-hint tabs show CSV/XML structure that doesn't match `data-contract.md`'s locked schema. Per CLAUDE.md, the skill won — tabs show the real contract.

**Design gaps** (also recorded in `docs/PLAN.md`): dropzone's third quick-fill button ("Try a broken file" in the design) became "Use sample with warnings" since there's no canonical corrupt-file asset — a more useful real-data substitution.

**What 4.3 (report view) will consume:**
- `GET /api/declarations/{id}` → `DeclarationDto` (already fetched by the stub page at `pages/DeclarationStubPage.tsx`) — has `perCategory[]`, `totalOutputVat`, `totalDeductibleInputVat`, `netVatPayable`, `validation.issues[]`, all typed in `api/types.ts`.
- `GET /api/declarations/{id}/pdf` — not yet wired to any button.
- `lib/declaration-status.ts` — status label/badge-variant mapping, reusable for the report header chip.
- The stub page's structure (`← Back to dashboard`, id + chip header, `Source · filename`) is the scaffold 4.3 extends with summary cards, the validation panel, and the category breakdown table.

**Open question for 4.3**: the design's report screen shows a fixed "Period · 2025 Q2 (Apr–Jun)" — there's no period/quarter concept anywhere in the backend (`DeclarationDto` has no date-range field). Worth deciding whether to compute one client-side from `createdAt`, add it server-side, or drop it from the report entirely.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

   This summary covers the tail end of a multi-session VATDesk (Hungarian VAT/ÁFA declaration generator) coding-challenge project. Three sessions are visible in full or near-full detail:

   **Phase 3 (backend domain, brief tail from prior context):** Complete the entire backend domain (Core models → parsers → validation V1-V8 → HU strategy → PDF → API endpoints) in 4 stages (A: registry+validation, B: parsers, C: strategy+persistence, D: PDF+API), each stage ending in green tests + one conventional commit. Explicit acceptance criteria included docker-compose curl verification and a `grep` check that no `double` type touches money math.

   **Phase 4.1 (auth + login + shell):** The user's prompt required: Stage A backend auth (seeded users with hashed passwords, JWT login/me endpoints, role policies matching the skill's API table, rate limiting on login, correct 401 vs 403 with ProblemDetails); Stage B frontend auth infrastructure (AuthContext with in-memory+sessionStorage token, API client wrapper with 401→redirect, RequireAuth/RequireRole guards); Stage C pages (/login matching the design pixel-conscientiously including all states — default/loading/invalid-credentials/empty-validation — and a Home/Dashboard placeholder with the app shell as the reusable frame for all future pages). A "DESIGN FIDELITY COMMITMENT" section required extracting design tokens into a central theme file, implementing light/dark theme with a toggle button (explicitly requested even though not in the design — user said "Consider using chadcn for this step. Also implement theme light/dark selection with button to change"), and building shared UI components in `frontend/src/components/ui/`. Constraints: UI role-gating is cosmetic only (server enforcement is the real rule), skill wins on conflict (must surface conflicts, not silently reconcile), boring choices + "Decisions made" list for anything uncovered, conventional commits per stage, final commit restructures docs/PLAN.md (Phase 5 baseline folded into 4.1, Entra ID kept as its own unchecked stretch line, Phase 4 sub-checkboxes 4.1-4.4).

   **Phase 4.2 (upload flow, the session immediately preceding this summary):** Verbatim scope from the user's prompt:
   - "Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, the hungarian-vat skill (SKILL.md + references/data-contract.md for the file rules), and study the Upload screen in docs/design/ — including the format hint tabs, sample download links, file card, inline error states, and the processing steps (Parsing → Validating → Calculating)."

   - **SCOPE BOUNDARY**: "The full report view is 4.3. This session ends at a stub: route /declarations/:id renders inside the app shell showing declaration id, status chip (per design status colors), and a 'Full report view coming soon' note. Success navigation targets this stub. Do not build summary cards, category tables, or the validation panel yet."
   - **Stage A** — Backend: serve canonical sample files via GET /api/samples/clean.csv, /invalid.csv, /nav.xml (any authenticated user), correct Content-Type/Content-Disposition; source of truth stays `.claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/` (must NOT duplicate files in git — copy via MSBuild step, Dockerfile must pick them up); add a byte-identical test; verify POST /api/declarations returns proper ProblemDetails for oversized/unsupported/empty files (fix any 500s found, note under "Decisions made").
   - **Stage B** — Upload page (/declarations/new, Admin-only via RequireRole): drag & drop + click-to-browse; client-side pre-validation before upload (size/empty/extension) as UX only, server remains enforcement; format hint tabs "CSV"/"NAV 3.0 XML" sourced from data-contract.md; "Download sample file" links for both formats; file card (name, size, remove) + Process button.
   - **Stage C** — Processing + outcomes: stepped progress state (Parsing→Validating→Calculating) as an "indeterminate visual sequence," with an explicit instruction to "be honest in code comments that steps are presentational, not server events"; success → navigate to /declarations/:id stub with a success toast showing status; failure paths each with designed states (400 unparseable → full error screen with sample links + Try again; 401 → existing redirect; 403 → "Admins only" notice; network failure → retryable error toast); wire dashboard's "New declaration" button (was "Coming soon") to /declarations/new, Admin-only.
   - **ACCEPTANCE**: frontend zero TS errors; dotnet test green including sample-serving and error-shape tests; docker compose up browser verification (download both samples, upload clean→Completed, upload invalid→CompletedWithWarnings, drop 6MB→inline rejection without network call, rename .png to .csv→server-side rejection with designed error screen); viewer route guard bounces + dashboard button absent.
   - **CONSTRAINTS**: skill wins on conflict (surface conflicts); boring choices + "Decisions made"; conventional commits per stage; final commit checks off 4.2 in docs/PLAN.md, adds new "Design gaps" found, and ends with "what exists, DTO/route additions 4.3 will consume, and open questions for the report view."

   A separate, standalone instruction appeared mid-session-2 (Phase 4.1) as a plain user message: **"Install it if not [available]"** — this was the user's explicit instruction to install Playwright (since I had said I lacked a browser tool for visual verification), which I did into the scratchpad directory rather than the project.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - ASP.NET Core 8 Web API, layered architecture (Api → Infrastructure → Core), EF Core + Npgsql, migrations auto-applied on startup (guarded by `IsRelational()` check for InMemory test compatibility).
   - JWT auth: `Microsoft.AspNetCore.Authentication.JwtBearer`, HS256, claims (`ClaimTypes.Role`, `ClaimTypes.Name`, `ClaimTypes.Email`, `ClaimTypes.NameIdentifier`), fail-fast key validation (≥32 bytes) at startup, `Microsoft.AspNetCore.Identity.PasswordHasher<TUser>` for hashing (no separate package needed in Api since transitively available via Infrastructure's `Microsoft.Extensions.Identity.Core` reference).
   - ASP.NET Core rate limiting (`Microsoft.AspNetCore.RateLimiting`, `AddFixedWindowLimiter`/`AddPolicy` with `RateLimitPartition.GetFixedWindowLimiter` partitioned by client IP).
   - `UseStatusCodePages()` + `AddProblemDetails()` combo to auto-convert bare 401/403 into ProblemDetails JSON.
   - .NET keyed DI services (`AddKeyedSingleton`, `[FromKeyedServices("HU")]`, `GetRequiredKeyedService`) — and the specific pitfall that keyed services don't thread through implicit constructor injection, requiring `ActivatorUtilities.CreateInstance` in a factory delegate.
   - MSBuild `Content` items with `Link`/`CopyToOutputDirectory`/`CopyToPublishDirectory` metadata for copying external files (skill assets) into build/publish output without duplicating them in git.
   - `AppContext.BaseDirectory` behavior under `WebApplicationFactory<Program>`-based in-process TestServer hosting — empirically verified to resolve correctly to the Api project's own output directory (not the test project's), so no extra workaround was needed.
   - React 19 + TypeScript + Vite 8 + React Router v7 (`react-router-dom`), Tailwind CSS v4 (`@tailwindcss/vite` plugin, `@theme inline` CSS-variable-driven design tokens, `@custom-variant dark`), shadcn-style component patterns (Radix UI primitives + `class-variance-authority` + `clsx`/`tailwind-merge` via a `cn()` utility), `lucide-react` icons.
   - React Context pattern for `AuthContext` (in-memory token/user with sessionStorage rehydration-on-mount only) and `ToastContext` (toast queue with auto-dismiss).
   - Cosmetic vs. real enforcement distinction repeatedly emphasized: `RequireRole` (inline UI hiding) and `RequireRoleRoute` (route-level bounce) are both explicitly documented as NOT security boundaries — the API's `[Authorize(Roles=...)]` is the only real enforcement.
   - Playwright (installed standalone into the scratchpad, NOT added to the project's `package.json`) used as the browser-automation/visual-verification tool since no browser tool was available by default in this environment; screenshots captured and read via the `Read` tool to visually confirm design fidelity.
   - "Surface the conflict, don't reconcile silently" principle from CLAUDE.md, applied concretely when the design's example data contradicted `data-contract.md`'s locked schema.

3. Files and Code Sections (Phase 4.2 session — most recent and most relevant for continuation):

   Backend:
   - `src/VatDesk.Api/Controllers/SamplesController.cs` (new) — `[Authorize]`-gated (any authenticated user), 3 explicit `[HttpGet("clean.csv")]`/`[HttpGet("invalid.csv")]`/`[HttpGet("nav.xml")]` actions calling a shared `ServeFile` helper that does `Path.Combine(AppContext.BaseDirectory, "samples", sourceFileName)` + `PhysicalFile(path, contentType, downloadFileName)` for correct Content-Disposition.
   - `src/VatDesk.Api/VatDesk.Api.csproj` — added 3 `<Content Include="..\..\.claude\skills\hungarian-vat\assets\sample-*.{csv,xml}">` items each with `<Link>samples\...</Link>`, `<CopyToOutputDirectory>PreserveNewest</CopyToOutputDirectory>`, `<CopyToPublishDirectory>PreserveNewest</CopyToPublishDirectory>`.
   - `Dockerfile` — added `COPY .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/ .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/` in the `api-build` stage (before `dotnet publish`), since previously only `src/` was copied and the relative-path Content items would have failed to resolve inside the Docker build context.
   - `tests/VatDesk.Tests/Api/SamplesApiTests.cs` (new) — byte-identical assertions for all 3 samples (compared against `SkillFixtures.Path(...)`), Content-Type/Content-Disposition checks, anonymous→401 test.
   - `tests/VatDesk.Tests/Api/DeclarationsUploadErrorTests.cs` (new) — `Upload_OversizedFile_ReturnsProblemDetailsNot500` (confirmed 400, not 413, via real Kestrel), `Upload_RandomBinaryContentWithCsvExtension_Returns400NotServerError`, `Upload_EmptyFile_Returns400ProblemDetails`, `Upload_WrongExtension_Returns400ProblemDetails` — all passed without any backend code changes needed (verified empirically against both TestServer and real docker-compose Kestrel).

   Frontend — new shared UI primitives:
   - `frontend/src/components/ui/tabs.tsx` (new) — Radix `@radix-ui/react-tabs` wrapper (`Tabs`, `TabsList`, `TabsTrigger`, `TabsContent`) styled with `data-[state=active]:border-primary data-[state=active]:bg-card` etc.
   - `frontend/src/components/ui/toast.tsx` (new) — presentational `ToastViewport` component, fixed bottom-right, colored left border per type (success/error/info → `--success`/`--destructive`/`--primary` tokens), icon circle, dismiss button.
   - `frontend/src/context/ToastContext.tsx` (new) — `ToastProvider`, `useToast()` hook, `addToast(type, title, message?, action?)`, auto-dismiss after 4200ms, exports `ToastItem`/`ToastAction`/`ToastType` types.

   Frontend — API client (`frontend/src/api/client.ts`, extended):
   ```ts
   export function uploadDeclaration(file: File, signal?: AbortSignal): Promise<DeclarationDto> {
     const formData = new FormData()
     formData.append('file', file)
     return apiFetch<DeclarationDto>('/api/declarations', { method: 'POST', body: formData, signal })
   }

   async function fetchSampleBlob(name: SampleFileName): Promise<Blob> { /* auth header + 401 handling, returns response.blob() */ }

   export async function fetchSampleAsFile(name: SampleFileName): Promise<File> {
     const blob = await fetchSampleBlob(name)
     const type = name.endsWith('.xml') ? 'application/xml' : 'text/csv'
     return new File([blob], `sample-${name}`, { type })
   }

   export async function downloadSample(name: SampleFileName): Promise<void> {
     /* fetch blob, create object URL, trigger <a download> click, revoke URL */
   }

   export function getDeclaration(id: string): Promise<DeclarationDto> {
     return apiFetch<DeclarationDto>(`/api/declarations/${id}`)
   }
   ```
   `SampleFileName` type = `'clean.csv' | 'invalid.csv' | 'nav.xml'`.

   Frontend — route guard:
   - `frontend/src/components/auth/RequireRoleRoute.tsx` (new) — route-level `<Outlet/>` wrapper that `<Navigate to="/" replace />`s if `user.role` doesn't match; explicitly documented as cosmetic, same as `RequireRole`.

   Frontend — Upload feature components (`frontend/src/components/upload/`, all new):
   - `DropZone.tsx` — drag/drop + click-to-browse, client validation (`MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES = 5*1024*1024`, `ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS = ['.csv','.xml']`), inline `Alert` on rejection, 3 quick-fill buttons: "Use sample .csv" (clean.csv), "Use sample .xml" (nav.xml), "Use sample with warnings" (invalid.csv — replacing the design's "Try a broken file").
   - `FileCard.tsx` — file icon/ext badge, name, size, Remove/Process buttons.
   - `FormatHintTabs.tsx` — Tabs component with **corrected** CSV/XML example content (see Errors/Fixes section below for the exact conflict), download links via `downloadSample('clean.csv'|'nav.xml')`.
   - `ProcessingScreen.tsx` — spinner + `STEP_LABELS = ['Parsing invoice rows', 'Validating against NAV rules', 'Calculating VAT totals']`, `currentStep: number` prop drives done/active/waiting visual states; explicit comment: "The real API is a single request/response — there is no server-sent progress... these steps are purely a presentational sequence timed to feel similar, not driven by anything the server reports."
   - `UploadErrorScreen.tsx` — full "We couldn't process that file" screen with checklist, sample download links, Back to dashboard / Try again buttons.

   Frontend — pages:
   - `frontend/src/pages/UploadPage.tsx` (new) — core state machine:
     ```ts
     type Phase =
       | { kind: 'select'; file: File | null }
       | { kind: 'processing'; file: File; step: number }
       | { kind: 'error'; fileName: string }
       | { kind: 'forbidden' }

     const STEP_DELAYS_MS = [1000, 2100]
     const MIN_DISPLAY_MS = 3200
     ```
     `process(file)` sets timers to advance `step` presentationally, races `Promise.all([uploadDeclaration(file), minDisplay])`, on success calls `addToast('success', 'Declaration ready', ...)` then `navigate(`/declarations/${dto.id}`)`; on `ApiError` with status 401 returns early (apiFetch already redirecting), 403 sets `{kind:'forbidden'}`, other statuses set `{kind:'error', fileName}`; on non-ApiError (network failure) shows a toast with a `{label:'Retry', onClick:() => process(file)}` action and resets to `{kind:'select', file}`.
   - `frontend/src/pages/DeclarationStubPage.tsx` (new) — fetches `getDeclaration(id)` on mount, states `loading|loaded|not-found|error`, renders id + status `Badge` (via `declarationStatusBadgeVariant`) + "Full report view coming soon." card; explicit comment: "Phase 4.2 scope boundary: full report view (summary cards, category table, validation panel) is Phase 4.3."
   - `frontend/src/lib/declaration-status.ts` (new) — `declarationStatusLabel(status)` and `declarationStatusBadgeVariant(status)` shared helpers mapping `DeclarationStatus` → display text / Badge variant (`success`/`warning`/`destructive`).

   Frontend — modified for wiring:
   - `frontend/src/App.tsx` — added `ToastProvider` wrapper, `/declarations/:id` route (inside `RequireAuth`+`AppShell`, any authenticated user), `/declarations/new` route wrapped in an additional `<Route element={<RequireRoleRoute role="Admin" />}>`.
   - `frontend/src/components/shell/Header.tsx` — replaced the disabled/tooltip "New declaration" nav button with a real `<Link to="/declarations/new">`, added `useLocation`-based active-state styling via a `navLinkClass(active)` helper.
   - `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.tsx` — replaced both `aria-disabled`/Tooltip CTA buttons ("New declaration" and "Create your first declaration") with real `onClick={() => navigate('/declarations/new')}` buttons wrapped in `RequireRole role="Admin"` / conditional `user?.role === 'Admin'`; added comment: "Declaration history/listing is Phase 4.4 — this still always shows the empty state, even after a real upload exists, until that session wires GET /api/declarations here."

   - `docs/PLAN.md` — checked off `[x] 4.2 — Upload flow (drag/drop, sample files, processing states)`; added to "Key API surface": `GET /api/samples/{clean.csv,invalid.csv,nav.xml} (any authenticated user)`; added a new "## Design gaps (accumulated across sessions)" section listing all 5 gaps found across 4.1 and 4.2 (dark mode, demo credential copy, UserEntity.DisplayName, format-hint tabs conflict, dropzone 3rd button substitution).

4. Errors and fixes (Phase 4.2 session specifically; Phase 4.1's DI/tooltip bugs are prior-session context but summarized for completeness since they remain live in the codebase):

   - **Design/skill schema conflict (format-hint tabs)**: The design's CSV example used `invoice_no,partner_name,partner_tax_id,direction,vat_category,net_huf,vat_huf` with `direction` values `sales|purchase`, and the XML example used a fake `<invoiceMain><lineVatRate><vatPercentage>` structure — none of which match `data-contract.md`'s actual locked schema (`InvoiceNumber,IssueDate,PartnerName,PartnerTaxNumber,Direction,NetAmount,VatCode,VatAmount,GrossAmount,Currency` with `Direction=OUT|IN`, and real XML `invoiceIssueDate`/`invoiceDirection`/`invoiceLines`/`line`/`lineVatData`/`vatPercentage|vatExemption`/`lineVatAmount`). Per CLAUDE.md's explicit hard rule ("skill wins on conflict, surface it"), I used the REAL skill schema in `FormatHintTabs.tsx` (with a code comment explaining the substitution) rather than copying the design's placeholder text verbatim. This was surfaced explicitly in the commit message and in docs/PLAN.md's new "Design gaps" section.
   - **No canonical "broken file" asset**: Design's 3rd dropzone button is "Try a broken file" (demos full structural parse failure), but the skill only ships `sample-clean.csv`, `sample-invalid.csv`, `sample-nav.xml` — no corrupt/unparseable asset exists. Rather than fabricating a fake file (which would violate "don't invent new visual styles"/asset scope), I substituted "Use sample with warnings" using the real `sample-invalid.csv`, which demonstrates a different but equally valid designed state (`CompletedWithWarnings`) using genuine data. The full-failure error screen remains fully implemented and reachable via any genuinely unparseable upload (verified via the renamed-PNG-as-.csv test).
   - **`AppContext.BaseDirectory` ambiguity under WebApplicationFactory**: Initially uncertain whether `SamplesController`'s `Path.Combine(AppContext.BaseDirectory, "samples", ...)` would resolve correctly inside the in-process TestServer host (which might use the TEST project's bin directory rather than the Api project's). Rather than guessing or defensively duplicating the MSBuild copy items into the test project, I wrote the `SamplesApiTests.cs` byte-identical test FIRST and ran it — it passed on the first try, empirically confirming `AppContext.BaseDirectory` resolves to the Api project's own output directory in this hosting scenario. No workaround was needed.
   - **Oversized-file behavior initially assumed risky (potential 500)**: The task explicitly warned this might currently produce a 500 and asked me to fix it if so. I wrote `Upload_OversizedFile_ReturnsProblemDetailsNot500` and ran it — it passed against the in-process TestServer, but I was skeptical since `TestServer` might not faithfully replicate real Kestrel's request-size enforcement. I then independently verified via `docker compose up` + `curl` with an actual 6MB file against the real running container, confirming the real response is `400` with `"title":"One or more validation errors occurred.","errors":{"":["Failed to read the request form. Request body too large..."]}` — a clean ASP.NET Core `[ApiController]`-automatic ProblemDetails response, never a 500. Also verified the renamed-PNG-as-.csv scenario and empty-file scenario directly via curl against the live container. Concluded and documented (in the commit message and code comment) that no backend fix was needed — the existing implementation already handles all these paths gracefully. Tightened the test assertion afterward from `RequestEntityTooLarge or BadRequest` to the more precise/documented `BadRequest` only, with a comment explaining this was verified against real Kestrel.
   - **Test suite rate-limiter collision (carried over pattern from Phase 4.1, reused correctly here)**: Not a new bug this session, but the pre-existing `VatDeskWebApplicationFactory.CreateAuthenticatedClientAsync(role)` caching pattern (login once per role, cache the token at the factory level) was reused correctly for all new Phase 4.2 tests to avoid re-tripping the shared login rate limiter (`PermitLimit=8`/min) across the many new test methods added in `SamplesApiTests.cs` and `DeclarationsUploadErrorTests.cs`.

   (For completeness, Phase 4.1 bugs already fixed and still live in the codebase, referenced but not re-fixed this session: the `AddCountry` keyed-DI bug fixed via `ActivatorUtilities.CreateInstance`, and the native-`disabled`-kills-tooltip accessibility bug fixed via `aria-disabled` + promoting the raw "Sign out" button to a proper Radix `DropdownMenuItem`.)

5. Problem Solving:
   - Confirmed via direct empirical testing (not speculation) that ASP.NET Core's `[ApiController]` automatic model-binding-failure handling already converts oversized-request-body failures, non-UTF8 binary content, empty files, and wrong extensions all into clean 400 ProblemDetails responses without any custom exception-handling code — this was verified against both the in-process `TestServer` (via `dotnet test`) and the real Kestrel server (via `docker compose up` + `curl` with genuine 6MB/binary/empty files), giving high confidence this holds in the actual deployed environment, not just the test harness.
   - Resolved the git-duplication-avoidance requirement for sample files ("Source of truth stays .claude/skills/hungarian-vat/assets/ — do NOT duplicate the files in git") using MSBuild `Content` items with `Link` + `CopyToOutputDirectory`/`CopyToPublishDirectory` metadata, verified to work correctly for both local `dotnet publish` (tested directly, files landed in `/tmp/vd-publish-test/samples/`) and inside the Docker multi-stage build (required fixing the Dockerfile's `api-build` stage, which previously didn't copy `.claude/` into the build context at all).

[Result: # VATDesk Input Data Contract

Two input formats are supported. Format is decided by content sniffing: a file whose
first non-whitespace character is `<` is treated as XML; otherwise CSV is attempted.
Extension is a hint, never the decider.

## 1. CSV contract

- Encoding: UTF-8 (accept BOM). Delimiter: comma. Header row **required**.
- Decimal separator: `.` — parse with invariant culture. Reject `,` decimals as a
  row error with a helpful message ("use 27000.50, not 27000,50").
- Dates: ISO `...]

    string DisplayNameHu,
    string DisplayNameEn,
    int SortOrder);

interface IVatCategoryRegistry
{
    string CountryCode { get; }          // "HU", "RO", ...

**Claude:**

## Phase 4.3 complete

**What exists**: the `/declarations/:id` stub is replaced with the full report — header (id, filename, processed date, status chip, Back/Download PDF), summary cards (Output/Input/Net VAT with the teal-dominant Net VAT Payable card, rows processed), a collapsible validation panel (severity pills, errors-before-warnings sorted by row, empty state for clean files), and the category breakdown table (Sales/Purchases grouping, All/Sales/Purchases filter, per-group subtotals, grand total, exempt/RC legend) — all driven by `GET /api/countries/HU/vat-categories` (cached), never hardcoded. No backend changes were needed — `DeclarationDto` already had everything.

**Verified in the browser** (docker compose): clean-sample upload lands on a report matching every golden value from `data-contract.md` exactly (94 300 / 50 600 / 43 700, all 8 category×direction rows, correct subtotals/grand total); invalid-sample shows `CompletedWithWarnings` with all rule ids/row numbers and confirms error rows are excluded from totals (Input VAT = 0); viewer opens both by URL with full render + PDF download and no admin affordances; unknown id shows the designed not-found state; dark mode renders correctly throughout (no hardcoded colors). One real bug caught by screenshot review and fixed: the legend was lowercasing "Intra-EU" into "intra-eu" — removed the `.toLowerCase()`.

**Design gaps logged**: hu-HU space-grouped money formatting (the skill's explicit rule) instead of the mockup's comma style; the "Period · 2025 Q2" line dropped (no such field in the data model — open question for a future session); registry's canonical category names used verbatim instead of the design's paraphrased ones; negative Net VAT Payable given a minimal same-card treatment since the mockup only shows the positive case.

**For 4.4**: `GET /api/declarations` already returns everything a history table needs; `declarationStatusLabel/Variant`, `formatAmount/formatDate`, and `downloadDeclarationPdf` are all shared and ready to reuse — no new backend or client work anticipated for a basic table.

**Claude:**

## Root cause confirmed and fixed

You were right — the dashboard never called `GET /api/declarations` at all. `DashboardPage.tsx` had a hardcoded empty state left over from before Phase 4.4 was built (there was even a comment saying exactly that).

**The fix:**
- Wired `getDeclarations()` into `DashboardPage.tsx` with proper loading/error/empty/loaded states, rendering a new `DeclarationsTable` component (matching the design's table: date, source file with format badge + id, status chip, net VAT payable, created by, View/PDF actions).

**A second, related bug found while wiring "Created by":** `DeclarationRepository.SaveAsync` hardcoded `UserId = null` with a stale comment ("no auth this session") from before JWT auth existed — so no upload has ever recorded who created it, even after Phase 4.1 added real login. Fixed by threading the authenticated user's id from the JWT claim through the controller into the repository, and exposing it as `createdByName` on the list DTO (via a new `.Include(d => d.User)`).

**Verified**: `dotnet test` 88/88 green (added a test asserting list-after-upload returns the correct declaration attributed to the uploader), frontend build clean, and a full docker-compose + Playwright pass confirming the dashboard now lists all 7 previously-uploaded declarations, View/PDF actions work, viewer sees the same list without admin affordances, and pre-fix rows correctly show "—" for creator (since that data genuinely can't be recovered).

**Human:**

Read CLAUDE.md, docs/PLAN.md, and the hungarian-vat skill — especially the 
11-point security checklist in references/architecture.md. This session is 
Phase 6: a security audit and hardening pass over the ENTIRE existing codebase. 
This is not a feature session. Work in three stages: AUDIT (no code changes), 
then FIX, then PROVE.

STAGE A — AUDIT (read-only; commit nothing yet)
Go through all 11 checklist items one by one. For each, produce a verdict table 
row: item | status (Implemented / Partial / Missing / N-A) | evidence (file + 
line/config reference) | gap if any. Do not trust memory of earlier sessions — 
verify in the actual code. Specific things to check per item:
 1. Upload limits: Kestrel MaxRequestBodySize AND explicit endpoint check AND 
    multipart section limit — all three, not just one. Extension allow-list and 
    content sniffing actually reject, not just log.
 2. XML: DtdProcessing.Prohibit + XmlResolver=null + char cap present in the 
    ACTIVE parser path (not just a helper nobody calls); the XXE test still 
    exists and fails if protection is removed (mutate mentally, or temporarily, 
    to confirm the test bites).
 3. Parsing: grep amount paths for double/float; confirm invariant culture on 
    every decimal/date parse including any frontend-supplied values.
 4. JWT: key from env only, startup fail-fast on missing/short key, sensible 
    expiry, HS256 explicitly pinned (no algorithm confusion), no key or 
    connection string anywhere in git history (git log -p search for obvious 
    patterns; report findings honestly).
 5. AuthZ: every endpoint listed in the skill's API table has the correct 
    policy attribute; no accidentally-anonymous endpoints (list ALL mapped 
    endpoints and their auth requirements — including /api/samples/* and 
    /api/health).
 6. Rate limiting: login AND upload endpoints; verify the partition key 
    (per-IP or per-user) is deliberate.
 7. CORS: locked to app origin; confirm prod single-origin serving makes it 
    moot but configured.
 8. Headers: HSTS, X-Content-Type-Options, X-Frame-Options DENY, minimal CSP — 
    check they're on ALL responses including static files and the SPA fallback. 
    CSP must not silently break the Vite-built app (inline styles/scripts?).
 9. Errors: throw a deliberate exception path in review — confirm ProblemDetails 
    without stack trace in prod mode; check dev-vs-prod behavior split; Serilog 
    (or equivalent) captures details server-side.
10. CSV export: we don't export CSV in v1 — mark N/A with a code comment where 
    an export would live, so the awareness is documented.
11. Secrets: .env git-ignored, docker-compose uses env vars, no secrets in 
    appsettings.json committed, README documents required env vars.
Also audit two things NOT on the checklist and report: (a) PDF endpoint — can a 
Viewer of one org read another user's declaration by guessing ids? We have no 
multi-tenancy, ids are GUIDs — state the reasoning and whether GUID 
non-enumerability is acceptable for demo scope; (b) dependency check — run 
dotnet list package --vulnerable and npm audit, report findings.

Present the full verdict table to me in the session output BEFORE moving to 
Stage B.

STAGE B — FIX
Fix every Partial/Missing item. Smallest correct change; do not refactor working 
protections for elegance. Each fix = its own conventional commit referencing the 
checklist item number (e.g., "fix(security): add X-Frame-Options and CSP headers 
[checklist #8]"). Vulnerable dependencies: update patch/minor versions only; if 
a fix requires a major bump, report instead of upgrading.

STAGE C — PROVE
- Add/extend tests so each testable item has a test that FAILS if the protection 
  is removed: oversized upload rejected, spoofed extension rejected, XXE 
  rejected, anonymous 401 on protected endpoints, Viewer 403 on admin endpoint, 
  login rate limit trips, error response contains no stack trace.
- Manual verification via docker compose in prod-like mode: curl -i the health, 
  login, and a static asset — paste the response headers into the session output 
  showing items #8/#9 live.
- Write docs/SECURITY.md: the checklist with final status per item, one line of 
  evidence each, the two extra audits (id enumeration reasoning, dependency 
  scan results), and known accepted risks for demo scope (sessionStorage JWT 
  tradeoff from 4.1, no multi-tenancy, demo credentials by design). Link it 
  from README's Security section.

ACCEPTANCE
- Verdict table delivered before any fix; all 11 items end Implemented or N/A 
  with evidence; all Stage C tests green; headers proven via pasted curl output; 
  SECURITY.md committed; docs/PLAN.md Phase 6 checked in the final commit with 
  a one-line summary of what was actually fixed vs already in place.

CONSTRAINTS
- Skill wins on conflict; surface conflicts. If an audit finding suggests the 
  skill's checklist itself has a gap, say so explicitly — do not silently 
  exceed or ignore scope.
- No new features, no refactors beyond what a fix strictly requires.
- Be honest in the verdict table: "Partial" findings about your own earlier 
  work are expected and are the point of this session.

[Result: # VATDesk Architecture & Conventions

## Stack

- Backend: ASP.NET Core 8 (LTS) Web API, EF Core + Npgsql, QuestPDF (Community license).
- Frontend: React 18 + TypeScript + Vite, served as static files by the API in
  production (single deployable unit).
- DB: PostgreSQL. Migrations applied automatically on startup.
- Packaging: multi-stage Dockerfile (node build → dotnet build → runtime image);
  docker-compose adds Postgres. Deployment target: Azure (Web App for Containers or
  Container Apps)...]

**Human:**

[Result: # VATDesk

Hungarian VAT (ÁFA) declaration generator. Ingests invoice/transaction files (CSV or
NAV 3.0-style XML), validates them, aggregates amounts by Hungarian VAT category, and
produces a declaration summary — on-screen and as a PDF.

<!-- TODO: one-paragraph pitch + screenshot once the UI is implemented (Phase 4) -->

## Overview

[Result: const STORAGE_KEY = 'vatdesk-theme'

export type Theme = 'light' | 'dark'

export function getStoredTheme(): Theme {
  const stored = localStorage.getItem(STORAGE_KEY)
  if (stored === 'light' || stored === 'dark') return stored
  return window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)').matches ? 'dark' : 'light'
}

export function applyTheme(theme: Theme) {
  document.documentElement.classList.toggle('dark', theme === 'dark')
  localStorage.setItem(STORAGE_KEY, theme)
}]

**Claude:**

Good — only the pre-existing user edit to PLAN.md, nothing else changed. I have everything needed for the full audit. Here's the Stage A verdict table.

## Stage A — Security Audit (read-only)

| # | Item | Status | Evidence | Gap |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Upload limits | **Partial** | `ParserFactory.MaxFileSizeBytes` (5MB) enforced via `[RequestSizeLimit]` on `DeclarationsController.Upload` ([DeclarationsController.cs:28](src/VatDesk.Api/Controllers/DeclarationsController.cs#L28)) + `FormOptions.MultipartBodyLengthLimit` ([Program.cs:27-28](src/VatDesk.Api/Program.cs#L27-L28)) + explicit `content.Length` check in `ParserFactory.ParseAsync` ([ParserFactory.cs:20-24](src/VatDesk.Infrastructure/Parsing/ParserFactory.cs#L20-L24)). Extension allow-list and content-sniffing both genuinely reject (400), verified via test + live curl. | **Kestrel's global `MaxRequestBodySize` is never explicitly configured** — relies solely on the per-endpoint `[RequestSizeLimit]` attribute. Defense-in-depth gap: any future endpoint that forgets the attribute falls back to Kestrel's default (~28.6 MB), not our 5 MB. |
| 2 | XML/XXE | **Implemented** | `NavXmlInvoiceParser.cs:26-28`: `DtdProcessing.Prohibit` + `XmlResolver = null` + `MaxCharactersInDocument = 5_000_000`, all in the one active parse path (no bypass helper). Verified live: temporarily downgraded `DtdProcessing.Prohibit`→`Parse` and re-ran `Upload_XxeAttempt_Returns400ProblemDetails` — **it still passed**, confirming `XmlResolver = null` alone already blocks the SYSTEM-entity payload (genuine defense-in-depth, not a single point of failure). Reverted immediately after. | None. |
| 3 | Parsing (decimal/invariant culture) | **Implemented** | `grep -rn "double\|float"` across `VatDesk.Core`/`VatDesk.Infrastructure` production code: zero hits. `FieldParsing.cs` uses `CultureInfo.InvariantCulture` for both decimal and date parsing; `CsvInvoiceParser` configures `CsvConfiguration(CultureInfo.InvariantCulture)`. Frontend never parses/re-computes amounts — only formats server-supplied numbers via `Intl.NumberFormat('hu-HU')`. | None. (One `double` appears only in a test's `[InlineData]` theory parameter, immediately cast to `decimal` before comparison — not a money-math path.) |
| 4 | JWT | **Partial** | Key sourced from `IConfiguration` only (env var `Jwt__Key` in docker-compose, never hardcoded in `appsettings.json`); fail-fast on missing/<32-byte key at startup ([Program.cs:47-54](src/VatDesk.Api/Program.cs#L47-L54)); 30-min expiry ([JwtOptions.cs](src/VatDesk.Api/Auth/JwtOptions.cs)); HS256 explicitly pinned on **issuance** (`SecurityAlgorithms.HmacSha256`). Git history search: no real leaked secret found — but **`docker-compose.yml` commits a working fallback JWT signing key** in git (`Jwt__Key: "${JWT_KEY:-lvFunuusnSO2w4AOAvJh7IVnyx4+AlnqpM78khacXx++Bl4a3flVQIAL15m8dY4u}"`), documented as demo-only but literally a usable secret in the repo. | (a) No explicit `ValidAlgorithms` restriction on the **validation** side — low practical risk since only a symmetric key exists (no RSA public key to enable classic alg-confusion), but not "explicitly pinned" per the letter of the checklist. (b) The committed fallback key violates "no key... in git" as literally read, even though it's clearly demo-scoped and documented. |
| 5 | AuthZ | **Implemented** | Full endpoint inventory: `POST /api/auth/login` → anonymous (by design) + rate-limited; `GET /api/auth/me` → `[Authorize]`; `GET /api/countries/{cc}/vat-categories` → `[Authorize]` (class-level); `POST /api/declarations` → `[Authorize(Roles="Admin")]`; `GET /api/declarations`, `GET /api/declarations/{id}`, `GET /api/declarations/{id}/pdf` → `[Authorize]` (any role); `GET /api/samples/*` → `[Authorize]` (any role); `GET /api/health` → **no `[Authorize]`**, intentionally anonymous (standard for LB health probes; leaks only assembly version + a DB-connected boolean — acceptable). All match the skill's API table exactly. No accidentally-anonymous endpoint found. | None — but the skill's own API table in `architecture.md` doesn't list `/api/samples/*` or `/api/health` at all (added in later sessions). Flagging as a **skill documentation gap**, not a code gap. |
| 6 | Rate limiting | **Missing** (upload) | `AddRateLimiter` policy `RateLimiterPolicies.Login` exists and is applied via `[EnableRateLimiting]` only on `AuthController.Login` ([AuthController.cs:26](src/VatDesk.Api/Controllers/AuthController.cs#L26)), partitioned deliberately by client IP (comment explains why: avoid one attacker locking out everyone on a shared IP). **No rate-limiting policy exists for `POST /api/declarations` (upload) at all.** | Upload endpoint has zero rate limiting — an authenticated Admin (or a leaked Admin token) can hammer the parse/PDF-render pipeline with unlimited requests. |
| 7 | CORS | **Missing** | No `AddCors`/`UseCors` anywhere in `Program.cs`. Moot in prod (API serves the built SPA from the same origin, only port 8080 exposed), but the skill explicitly says "still configured." | Not configured at all, even as an explicit no-op/locked policy. |
| 8 | Headers | **Missing** | No HSTS beyond `UseHttpsRedirection()` (no `UseHsts()`), no `X-Content-Type-Options`, no `X-Frame-Options`, no CSP anywhere in the codebase (`grep` for all four terms: zero hits outside this audit). | Fully missing. **Also found while investigating**: the built `frontend/index.html` has an inline `<script>` (pre-paint theme-flash prevention) with no nonce/hash — a strict `script-src 'self'` CSP would silently break it. It also loads Google Fonts cross-origin (`fonts.googleapis.com` / `fonts.gstatic.com`), and Radix UI (dropdown/tooltip) injects inline `style` attributes at runtime for positioning — both need explicit CSP allowances or they break silently. Real, concrete "CSP breaks the app" risks the audit specifically asked me to check for. |
| 9 | Errors | **Implemented** | `GlobalExceptionHandler` ([ErrorHandling/GlobalExceptionHandler.cs](src/VatDesk.Api/ErrorHandling/GlobalExceptionHandler.cs)) always returns a generic `ProblemDetails` (no stack trace, no exception message) and logs full details server-side via `ILogger` — **unconditionally**, not just in prod (stricter than required, no dev-mode leak path exists since no `UseDeveloperExceptionPage()` is registered). `UseStatusCodePages()` converts bare 401/403/404 into ProblemDetails too. No Serilog, but default `Microsoft.Extensions.Logging` (Console provider) is present and functionally equivalent for this scope. | None. |
| 10 | CSV export | **N/A** | No CSV export exists in v1 (declaration output is PDF only, per `docs/PLAN.md` locked decision). | Will add a documenting code comment at the natural location (`IReportRenderer`/near `DeclarationsController`) in Stage B per the task's explicit instruction, so the awareness is on record for whenever export is added. |
| 11 | Secrets | **Partial** | `.env` is git-ignored (`.gitignore:24-25`), `.env.example` is tracked with placeholders and generation instructions (`openssl rand -base64 48`), docker-compose consumes `${JWT_KEY}`/`${POSTGRES_*}` via env-var substitution, `appsettings.json`'s connection string is a trivial local-only `vatdesk:vatdesk` default (overridden by env var in docker-compose) — not a real secret. | Same finding as #4: the **fallback default value baked into `docker-compose.yml`** for `JWT_KEY` is, read literally, a committed secret — even though it's clearly demo-scoped, commented, and low-severity. README's Security section is still a `<!-- TODO -->` placeholder (Phase 6 hasn't landed yet). |

**Two additional audits (not on the checklist):**

**(a) PDF/declaration id enumeration** — `GET /api/declarations/{id}` and `/pdf` have no ownership check (`DeclarationRepository.GetByIdAsync` doesn't filter by `UserId`); any authenticated user (Admin or Viewer) can fetch any declaration by GUID. **This is intended, not a bug**: the app has no multi-tenancy — it's one shared workspace, and `GET /api/declarations` already returns the *entire unfiltered list* to every authenticated Viewer. A Viewer guessing an id gains nothing they don't already have via the list endpoint. GUID non-enumerability is irrelevant here because the real (and correctly enforced) boundary is "must be authenticated," not "must own this record." Acceptable for demo scope — becomes a real question only if multi-tenancy is ever added, which is out of this session's scope.

**(b) Dependency scan** —
- `dotnet list package --vulnerable --include-transitive`: **VatDesk.Core/.Infrastructure/.Api clean.** `VatDesk.Tests` flags `System.Net.Http 4.3.0` and `System.Text.RegularExpressions 4.3.0` (both High) — traced via `dotnet nuget why` to `xunit 2.5.3` → `NETStandard.Library 1.6.1`, a netstandard1.x compatibility metapackage. These shim assemblies are never loaded at runtime on .NET 8 (real BCL is used instead) and only affect the test project, never the shipped image — low practical risk, but a real, fixable transitive advisory. Verified bumping `xunit` → `2.9.3` and `xunit.runner.visualstudio` → `2.8.2` (still major version 2, so within the "patch/minor only" constraint) fully clears it with all 88 tests still green.
- `npm audit`: **0 vulnerabilities.**

**Summary going into Stage B**: 6 Implemented, 1 N/A, 4 Partial (#1, #4, #6, #11 — note #6 is really Missing for upload specifically), 1 Missing (#8), plus the xunit dependency fix and the CSP/inline-script frontend risk found during #8's investigation. Moving to Stage B now to fix all of these as individually-committed, minimally-scoped changes.

**Claude:**

Found a real bug I just introduced: `UseRateLimiter()` runs *before* `UseAuthentication()` in the pipeline, so the upload policy's `httpContext.User.FindFirstValue(ClaimTypes.NameIdentifier)` would always see an unauthenticated principal and silently fall back to IP-based partitioning — not the per-user partitioning I claimed. Let me fix the ordering.

**Claude:**

A deeper finding: I confirmed via an isolated repro that `UseHsts()` only sets the header when `Request.IsHttps` is true. That's fine for direct TLS, but since Azure Web App for Containers/Container Apps (the documented deployment target) terminate TLS at the platform edge and forward plain HTTP to the container, HSTS would never fire in the real deployment without forwarded-header awareness. Let me fix that.

---

**Claude:**

[Tool: Bash — rm -rf /tmp/hsts-repro]

**Human:**

[Result: (Bash completed with no output)]
